href="https://www.boston.gov/">Boston.gov</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Boston</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Massachusetts" title="List of municipalities in Massachusetts">most populous</a> municipality<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The city proper covers 48 square miles (124&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) with an estimated population of 685,094 in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-quickfacts_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quickfacts-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> making it also the most populous city in the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Boston is the seat of <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Suffolk County, Massachusetts">Suffolk County</a> as well, although the county government was disbanded on July 1, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The city is the economic and cultural anchor of a substantially larger metropolitan area known as <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical area</a> (MSA) home to a census-estimated 4.8&#160;million people in 2016 and ranking as the tenth-largest such area in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonMetroPopulation_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonMetroPopulation-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">combined statistical area</a> (CSA), this wider commuting region is home to some 8.2&#160;million people, making it the sixth-largest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston is one of the oldest cities in the United States, founded on the <a href="/wiki/Shawmut_Peninsula" title="Shawmut Peninsula">Shawmut Peninsula</a> in 1630 by <a href="/wiki/Puritans" title="Puritans">Puritan</a> settlers from England.<sup id="cite_ref-history_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy199411\xe2\x80\x9312_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy199411\xe2\x80\x9312-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> It was the scene of several key events of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Massacre" title="Boston Massacre">Boston Massacre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party" title="Boston Tea Party">Boston Tea Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bunker_Hill" title="Battle of Bunker Hill">Battle of Bunker Hill</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Boston" title="Siege of Boston">Siege of Boston</a>. Upon U.S. independence from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, it continued to be an important port and manufacturing hub as well as a center for education and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-AboutBoston_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AboutBoston-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris20058_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris20058-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The city has expanded beyond the original <a href="/wiki/Boston_Neck" title="Boston Neck">peninsula</a> through land reclamation and municipal annexation. Its rich history attracts many tourists, with <a href="/wiki/Faneuil_Hall" title="Faneuil Hall">Faneuil Hall</a> alone drawing more than 20&#160;million visitors per year.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonTourism_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonTourism-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s many firsts include the United States\' first public or <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">state school</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_School" title="Boston Latin School">Boston Latin School</a>, 1635),<sup id="cite_ref-BPS_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> first subway system (<a href="/wiki/Tremont_Street_Subway" title="Tremont Street Subway">Tremont Street Subway</a>, 1897),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull201142_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull201142-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and first public park (<a href="/wiki/Boston_Common" title="Boston Common">Boston Common</a>, 1634).\n</p><p>The Boston area\'s many <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Boston" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston">colleges and universities</a> make it an international center of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AcademicRanking2_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AcademicRanking2-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> including law, medicine, engineering, and business, and the city is considered to be a world leader in <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a>, with nearly 2,000 startups.<sup id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalBoston1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalBoston1-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kirsner_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirsner-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s economic base also includes finance,<sup id="cite_ref-BostonFinance_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonFinance-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> professional and business services, biotechnology, information technology, and government activities.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Households in the city claim the highest average rate of <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropy</a> in the United States;<sup id="cite_ref-transfer_of_wealth_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transfer_of_wealth-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> businesses and institutions rank among the top in the country for environmental <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> and investment.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The city has one of the highest <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">costs of living</a> in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heudorfer_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heudorfer-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> as it has undergone <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> though it remains high on world livability rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-quality_of_living_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quality_of_living-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label and politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Infrastructure"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Infrastructure</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">20</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Boston" title="History of Boston">History of Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Boston" title="Timeline of Boston">Timeline of Boston</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial">Colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_(NYPL_Hades-250999-465401).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg/220px-A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg/330px-A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg/440px-A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_%28NYPL_Hades-250999-465401%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5340" data-file-height="3845" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_south_east_view_of_the_great_town_of_Boston_in_New_England_in_America_(NYPL_Hades-250999-465401).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>A south east view of the great town of Boston in New England in America</i>, c. 1730</div></div></div>\n<p>Boston\'s early European settlers had first called the area <i>Trimountaine</i> (after its "three mountains," only traces of which remain today) but later renamed it <i>Boston</i> after <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Lincolnshire" title="Boston, Lincolnshire">Boston, Lincolnshire</a>, England, the origin of several prominent colonists. The renaming on September 7, 1630, (<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">Old Style</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> was by <a href="/wiki/Puritans" title="Puritans">Puritan</a> colonists from England<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy199411\xe2\x80\x9312_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy199411\xe2\x80\x9312-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> who had moved over from <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Boston" title="Charlestown, Boston">Charlestown</a> earlier that year in quest of fresh water. Their settlement was initially limited to the <a href="/wiki/Shawmut_Peninsula" title="Shawmut Peninsula">Shawmut Peninsula</a>, at that time surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay" title="Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a> and connected to the mainland by a narrow <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">isthmus</a>. The peninsula is thought to have been inhabited as early as 5000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1629, the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a>\'s first governor <a href="/wiki/John_Winthrop" title="John Winthrop">John Winthrop</a> led the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Agreement" title="Cambridge Agreement">Cambridge Agreement</a>, a key founding document of the city. Puritan ethics and their focus on education influenced its early history;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristopher200646_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristopher200646-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> America\'s first public school was founded in Boston in 1635.<sup id="cite_ref-BPS_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Over the next 130 years, the city participated in four <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">French and Indian Wars</a>, until the British defeated the French and their Indian allies in North America.\n</p><p>Boston was the largest town in <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a> until <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> grew larger in the mid-18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s <a href="/wiki/Shore" title="Shore">oceanfront location</a> made it a lively <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a>, and the city primarily engaged in <a href="/wiki/Shipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping">shipping</a> and fishing during its colonial days. However, Boston stagnated in the decades prior to the Revolution. By the mid-18th century, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and Philadelphia surpassed Boston in wealth. Boston encountered financial difficulties even as other cities in New England grew rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-newamernation_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newamernation-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-empireontheedge_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empireontheedge-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_the_Siege_of_Boston">Revolution and the Siege of Boston</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Revolution and the Siege of Boston">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Boston_campaign" title="Boston campaign">Boston campaign</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Boston" title="Siege of Boston">Siege of Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg/260px-Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg" width="260" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg/390px-Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg/520px-Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Tea_Party_w.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1773, a group of Boston rebels threw a shipment of tea by the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> into Boston Harbor as a response to the <a href="/wiki/Tea_Act" title="Tea Act">Tea Act</a>, in an event known as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party" title="Boston Tea Party">Boston Tea Party</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:30%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output boisterous the next day and night, giving the enemy time to improve their works, to bring up their cannon, and to put themselves in such a state of defence, that I could promise myself little success in attacking them under all the disadvantages I had to encounter \xe2\x80\xa6</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/William_Howe,_5th_Viscount_Howe" title="William Howe, 5th Viscount Howe">William Howe, 5th Viscount Howe</a>,&#32;in a letter to <a href="/wiki/William_Legge,_2nd_Earl_of_Dartmouth" title="William Legge, 2nd Earl of Dartmouth">William Legge, 2nd Earl of Dartmouth</a> about the British army\'s decision to leave Boston, dated March 21, 1776.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston,_1775bsmall1.png" class="image"><img alt="Map of Boston in 1775" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png/170px-Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png/255px-Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png/340px-Boston%2C_1775bsmall1.png 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="3500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston,_1775bsmall1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing a British tactical evaluation of Boston in 1775</div></div></div>\n<p>Many of the crucial events of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris20057_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris20057-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> occurred in or near Boston. Boston\'s penchant for mob action along with the colonists\' growing distrust in Britain fostered a revolutionary spirit in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-newamernation_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newamernation-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> When the British government passed the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_1765" title="Stamp Act 1765">Stamp Act</a> in 1765, a Boston mob ravaged the homes of <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Oliver" title="Andrew Oliver">Andrew Oliver</a>, the official tasked with enforcing the Act, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hutchinson_(governor)" title="Thomas Hutchinson (governor)">Thomas Hutchinson</a>, then the Lieutenant Governor of Massachusetts.<sup id="cite_ref-newamernation_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newamernation-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The British sent two regiments to Boston in 1768 in an attempt to quell the angry colonists. This did not sit well with the colonists. In 1770, during the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Massacre" title="Boston Massacre">Boston Massacre</a>, the army killed several people in response to a mob in Boston. The colonists compelled the British to withdraw their troops. The event was widely publicized and fueled a revolutionary movement in America.<sup id="cite_ref-empireontheedge_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empireontheedge-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1773, Britain passed the <a href="/wiki/Tea_Act" title="Tea Act">Tea Act</a>. Many of the colonists saw the act as an attempt to force them to accept the taxes established by the <a href="/wiki/Townshend_Acts" title="Townshend Acts">Townshend Acts</a>. The act prompted the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party" title="Boston Tea Party">Boston Tea Party</a>, where a group of rebels threw an entire shipment of tea sent by the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> into <a href="/wiki/Boston_Harbor" title="Boston Harbor">Boston Harbor</a>. The Boston Tea Party was a key event leading up to the revolution, as the British government responded furiously with the <a href="/wiki/Intolerable_Acts" title="Intolerable Acts">Intolerable Acts</a>, demanding compensation for the lost tea from the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-newamernation_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newamernation-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> This angered the colonists further and led to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. The war began in the area surrounding Boston with the <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Lexington_and_Concord" title="Battles of Lexington and Concord">Battles of Lexington and Concord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newamernation_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newamernation-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frothingham_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frothingham-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston itself was besieged for almost a year during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Boston" title="Siege of Boston">Siege of Boston</a>, which began on April 19, 1775. The New England militia impeded the movement of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Howe,_5th_Viscount_Howe" title="William Howe, 5th Viscount Howe">William Howe, 5th Viscount Howe</a>, then the commander-in-chief of the British forces in North America, led the British army in the siege. On June 17, the British captured the <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Boston" title="Charlestown, Boston">Charlestown peninsula</a> in Boston, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bunker_Hill" title="Battle of Bunker Hill">Battle of Bunker Hill</a>. The British army outnumbered the militia stationed there, but it was a <a href="/wiki/Pyrrhic_victory" title="Pyrrhic victory">Pyrrhic victory</a> for the British because their army suffered devastating casualties. It was also a testament to the power and courage of the militia, as their stubborn defending made it difficult for the British to capture Charlestown without losing many troops.<sup id="cite_ref-allemn_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allemn-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1776book_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1776book-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several weeks later, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> took over the militia after the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> to unify the revolutionary effort. Both sides faced difficulties and supply shortages in the siege, and the fighting was limited to small-scale raids and skirmishes. On March 4, 1776, Washington commanded his army to <a href="/wiki/Fortification_of_Dorchester_Heights" title="Fortification of Dorchester Heights">fortify Dorchester Heights</a>, an area of Boston. The army placed cannons there to repel a British invasion against their stake in Boston. Washington was confident that the army would be able to resist a small-scale invasion with their fortifications. Howe planned an invasion into Boston, but bad weather delayed their advance. Howe decided to withdraw, because the storm gave Washington\'s army more time to improve their fortifications. British troops evacuated Boston on March 17, which solidified the revolutionaries\' control of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-frothingham_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frothingham-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allemn_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allemn-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-revolution_and_the_War_of_1812">Post-revolution and the War of 1812</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-revolution and the War of 1812">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_State_House_and_State_Street,_Boston_1801.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg/220px-Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg/330px-Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg/440px-Old_State_House_and_State_Street%2C_Boston_1801.jpg 2x" data-file-width="738" data-file-height="547" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_State_House_and_State_Street,_Boston_1801.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/State_Street_(Boston)" title="State Street (Boston)">State Street</a>, 1801</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="Painting with a body of water with sailing ships in the foreground and a city in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg/220px-Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg/330px-Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg/440px-Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1345" data-file-height="907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston-view-1841-Havell.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Boston from <a href="/wiki/Dorchester_Heights" title="Dorchester Heights">Dorchester Heights</a>, 1841</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Revolution, Boston\'s long seafaring tradition helped make it one of the world\'s wealthiest international ports, with the slave trade,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> rum, fish, salt, and tobacco being particularly important.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s harbor activity was significantly curtailed by the <a href="/wiki/Embargo_Act_of_1807" title="Embargo Act of 1807">Embargo Act of 1807</a> (adopted during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. Foreign trade returned after these hostilities, but Boston\'s merchants had found alternatives for their capital investments in the interim. Manufacturing became an important component of the city\'s economy, and the city\'s industrial manufacturing overtook international trade in economic importance by the mid-19th century. Boston remained one of the nation\'s largest manufacturing centers until the early 20th century, and was known for its garment production and leather-goods industries.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A network of small rivers bordering the city and connecting it to the surrounding region facilitated shipment of goods and led to a proliferation of mills and factories. Later, a dense network of railroads furthered the region\'s industry and commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy199446_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy199446-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png/220px-TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png/330px-TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png/440px-TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png 2x" data-file-width="815" data-file-height="705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TremontSt_ca1843_Boston_byPhilipHarry_MFABoston.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tremont_Street" title="Tremont Street">Tremont Street</a>, 1843</div></div></div>\n<p>During this period, Boston flourished culturally, as well, admired for its <a href="/wiki/Classic_book" title="Classic book">rarefied literary life</a> and generous <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">artistic patronage</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BosLitHist_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BosLitHist-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BosLitHistMap_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BosLitHistMap-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> with members of old Boston families\xe2\x80\x94eventually dubbed <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Brahmin" title="Boston Brahmin">Boston Brahmins</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94coming to be regarded as the nation\'s social and cultural elites.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy199444_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy199444-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston was an early port of the <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">Atlantic triangular slave trade</a> in the New England colonies, but was soon overtaken by <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Massachusetts" title="Salem, Massachusetts">Salem, Massachusetts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Boston eventually became a center of the <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolitionist</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The city reacted strongly to the <a href="/wiki/Fugitive_Slave_Act_of_1850" title="Fugitive Slave Act of 1850">Fugitive Slave Act of 1850</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> contributing to President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce" title="Franklin Pierce">Franklin Pierce</a>\'s attempt to make an example of Boston after the <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Burns" title="Anthony Burns">Anthony Burns</a> Fugitive Slave Case.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1822,<sup id="cite_ref-AboutBoston_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AboutBoston-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> the citizens of Boston voted to change the official name from the "Town of Boston" to the "City of Boston", and on March 4, 1822, the people of Boston accepted the charter incorporating the City.<sup id="cite_ref-city_charter_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-city_charter-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> At the time Boston was chartered as a city, the population was about 46,226, while the area of the city was only 4.7 square miles (12&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-city_charter_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-city_charter-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1800_beacon_hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1800_beacon_hill.jpg/220px-1800_beacon_hill.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1800_beacon_hill.jpg/330px-1800_beacon_hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1800_beacon_hill.jpg/440px-1800_beacon_hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1800_beacon_hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cutting down Beacon Hill in 1811; a view from the north toward the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_State_House" title="Massachusetts State House">Massachusetts State House</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_City_Hall_(Boston).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg/220px-Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg/330px-Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg/440px-Old_City_Hall_%28Boston%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_City_Hall_(Boston).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_City_Hall_(Boston)" title="Old City Hall (Boston)">Old City Hall</a> was home to the Boston city council from 1865 to 1969.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_Square.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Colored print image of a city square in the 1900s" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_Square.JPG/220px-Haymarket_Square.JPG" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_Square.JPG/330px-Haymarket_Square.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_Square.JPG/440px-Haymarket_Square.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3270" data-file-height="2091" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_Square.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Square_(Boston)" title="Haymarket Square (Boston)">Haymarket Square</a>, 1909</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1820s, Boston\'s population grew rapidly, and the city\'s ethnic composition changed dramatically with the first wave of European <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigrants</a>. Irish immigrants dominated the first wave of newcomers during this period, especially following the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Irish Potato Famine</a>; by 1850, about 35,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_Irish_Americans_in_Boston" title="History of Irish Americans in Boston">Irish lived in Boston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In the latter half of the 19th century, the city saw increasing numbers of Irish, Germans, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>, Syrians,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_Canadians" title="French Canadians">French Canadians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia" title="History of the Jews in Russia">Russian</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">Polish Jews</a> settling in the city. By the end of the 19th century, Boston\'s core neighborhoods had become enclaves of ethnically distinct immigrants. Italians inhabited the <a href="/wiki/North_End,_Boston" title="North End, Boston">North End</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Irish dominated <a href="/wiki/South_Boston" title="South Boston">South Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Boston" title="Charlestown, Boston">Charlestown</a>, and Russian Jews lived in the <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Boston" title="West End, Boston">West End</a>. <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">Italian</a> immigrants brought with them Roman Catholicism. Currently, Catholics make up Boston\'s largest religious community,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and the Irish have played a major role in Boston politics since the early 20th century; prominent figures include the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">Kennedys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tip_O%27Neill" title="Tip O&#39;Neill">Tip O\'Neill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Fitzgerald" title="John F. Fitzgerald">John F. Fitzgerald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolino2012285\xe2\x80\x93286_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolino2012285\xe2\x80\x93286-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1631 and 1890, the city tripled its area through <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> by filling in marshes, mud flats, and gaps between wharves along the waterfront.<sup id="cite_ref-landfills_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landfills-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The largest reclamation efforts took place during the 19th century; beginning in 1807, the crown of Beacon Hill was used to fill in a 50-acre (20&#160;ha) mill pond that later became the <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Square_(Boston)" title="Haymarket Square (Boston)">Haymarket Square</a> area. The present-day <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_State_House" title="Massachusetts State House">State House</a> sits atop this lowered Beacon Hill. Reclamation projects in the middle of the century created significant parts of the <a href="/wiki/South_End,_Boston" title="South End, Boston">South End</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Boston" title="West End, Boston">West End</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Boston" title="Financial District, Boston">Financial District</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Boston" title="Chinatown, Boston">Chinatown</a>.\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Great_Boston_fire_of_1872" title="Great Boston fire of 1872">Great Boston fire of 1872</a>, workers used building rubble as landfill along the downtown waterfront. During the mid-to-late 19th century, workers filled almost 600 acres (2.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of brackish Charles River marshlands west of <a href="/wiki/Boston_Common" title="Boston Common">Boston Common</a> with gravel brought by rail from the hills of Needham Heights. The city annexed the adjacent towns of <a href="/wiki/South_Boston" title="South Boston">South Boston</a> (1804), <a href="/wiki/East_Boston" title="East Boston">East Boston</a> (1836), <a href="/wiki/Roxbury,_Boston" title="Roxbury, Boston">Roxbury</a> (1868), <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Boston" title="Dorchester, Boston">Dorchester</a> (including present-day <a href="/wiki/Mattapan" title="Mattapan">Mattapan</a> and a portion of <a href="/wiki/South_Boston" title="South Boston">South Boston</a>) (1870), <a href="/wiki/Brighton,_Boston" title="Brighton, Boston">Brighton</a> (including present-day <a href="/wiki/Allston" title="Allston">Allston</a>) (1874), <a href="/wiki/West_Roxbury" title="West Roxbury">West Roxbury</a> (including present-day <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Plain" title="Jamaica Plain">Jamaica Plain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roslindale" title="Roslindale">Roslindale</a>) (1874), <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Boston" title="Charlestown, Boston">Charlestown</a> (1874), and <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Boston" title="Hyde Park, Boston">Hyde Park</a> (1912).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Other proposals were unsuccessful for the annexation of <a href="/wiki/Boston%E2%80%93Brookline_annexation_debate_of_1873" title="Boston\xe2\x80\x93Brookline annexation debate of 1873">Brookline</a>, Cambridge,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_Massachusetts" title="Chelsea, Massachusetts">Chelsea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The city went into decline by the early to mid-20th century, as factories became old and obsolete and businesses moved out of the region for cheaper labor elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBluestoneStevenson200213_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBluestoneStevenson200213-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Boston responded by initiating various <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> projects, under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Planning_and_Development_Agency" title="Boston Planning and Development Agency">Boston Redevelopment Authority</a> (BRA) established in 1957. In 1958, BRA initiated a project to improve the historic West End neighborhood. Extensive demolition was met with strong public opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The BRA subsequently re-evaluated its approach to urban renewal in its future projects, including the construction of <a href="/wiki/Government_Center,_Boston" title="Government Center, Boston">Government Center</a>. In 1965, the Columbia Point Health Center opened in the <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Boston" title="Dorchester, Boston">Dorchester</a> neighborhood, the first <a href="/wiki/Community_health_centers_in_the_United_States" title="Community health centers in the United States">Community Health Center</a> in the United States. It mostly served the massive <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Point_(Boston)" class="mw-redirect" title="Columbia Point (Boston)">Columbia Point</a> public housing complex adjoining it, which was built in 1953. The health center is still in operation and was rededicated in 1990 as the Geiger-Gibson Community Health Center.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The Columbia Point complex itself was redeveloped and revitalized from 1984 to 1990 into a mixed-income residential development called Harbor Point Apartments.<sup id="cite_ref-Roessner_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roessner-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the 1970s, the city\'s economy had recovered after 30 years of economic downturn. A large number of high-rises were constructed in the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Boston" title="Financial District, Boston">Financial District</a> and in Boston\'s <a href="/wiki/Back_Bay,_Boston" title="Back Bay, Boston">Back Bay</a> during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy1994195_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy1994195-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> This boom continued into the mid-1980s and resumed after a few pauses. Hospitals such as <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Hospital" title="Massachusetts General Hospital">Massachusetts General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beth_Israel_Deaconess_Medical_Center" title="Beth Israel Deaconess Medical Center">Beth Israel Deaconess Medical Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brigham_and_Women%27s_Hospital" title="Brigham and Women&#39;s Hospital">Brigham and Women\'s Hospital</a> lead the nation in medical innovation and patient care. Schools such as <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School" title="Harvard Medical School">Harvard Medical School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Tufts University School of Medicine">Tufts University School of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_College_of_Art_and_Design" title="Massachusetts College of Art and Design">Massachusetts College of Art and Design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wentworth_Institute_of_Technology" title="Wentworth Institute of Technology">Wentworth Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music" title="Berklee College of Music">Berklee College of Music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Conservatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Conservatory">Boston Conservatory</a> attract students to the area. Nevertheless, the city experienced conflict starting in 1974 over <a href="/wiki/Desegregation_busing" title="Desegregation busing">desegregation busing</a>, which resulted in unrest and violence around public schools throughout the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy1994194\xe2\x80\x93195_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy1994194\xe2\x80\x93195-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg/220px-Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg/330px-Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg/440px-Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4706" data-file-height="3123" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Back_Bay_reflection.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Back_Bay,_Boston" title="Back Bay, Boston">Back Bay</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Boston is an intellectual, technological, and political center but has lost some important regional institutions,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> including the loss to mergers and acquisitions of local financial institutions such as <a href="/wiki/FleetBoston_Financial" title="FleetBoston Financial">FleetBoston Financial</a>, which was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Boston-based department stores <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Marsh" title="Jordan Marsh">Jordan Marsh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filene%27s" title="Filene&#39;s">Filene\'s</a> have both merged into the Cincinnati\xe2\x80\x93based <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s,_Inc." title="Macy&#39;s, Inc.">Macy\'s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\nThe 1993 acquisition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> was reversed in 2013 when it was re-sold to Boston businessman <a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John W. Henry</a>. In 2016, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> would be moving its corporate headquarters from Connecticut to the Innovation District in South Boston, joining many other companies in this rapidly developing neighborhood.\n</p><p>Boston has experienced <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a> in the latter half of the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> with housing prices increasing sharply since the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Heudorfer_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heudorfer-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Living expenses have risen; Boston has one of the highest costs of living in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and was ranked the 129th-most expensive major city in the world in a 2011 survey of 214 cities.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Despite cost-of-living issues, Boston ranks high on livability ratings, ranking 36th <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_liveable_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s most liveable cities">worldwide in quality of living</a> in 2011 in a survey of 221 major cities.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 15, 2013, two Chechen Islamist brothers <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombing" title="Boston Marathon bombing">detonated a pair of bombs</a> near the finish line of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Boston_Marathon" title="2013 Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a>, killing three people and injuring roughly 264.<sup id="cite_ref-260herald_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260herald-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Boston briefly <a href="/wiki/Boston_bid_for_the_2024_Summer_Olympics" title="Boston bid for the 2024 Summer Olympics">shouldered a bid</a> as the US applicant for the <a href="/wiki/2024_Summer_Olympics" title="2024 Summer Olympics">2024 Summer Olympics</a>. The bid was supported by the mayor and a coalition of business leaders and local philanthropists, but was eventually dropped due to public opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" title="United States Olympic Committee">USOC</a> then selected <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> to be the American candidate with Los Angeles ultimately securing the right to host the <a href="/wiki/2028_Summer_Olympics" title="2028 Summer Olympics">2028 Summer Olympics</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aerial view of the Boston area from space" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg/220px-Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg/330px-Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg/440px-Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Massachusetts_2007_satellite_photo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boston as seen from the International Space Station (ISS)</div></div></div>\n<p>Boston has an area of 89.63 square miles (232.1&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)\xe2\x80\x9448.4 square miles (125.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (54.0%) of land and 41.2 square miles (106.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (46.0%) of water. The city\'s official elevation, as measured at <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan International Airport</a>, is 19&#160;ft (5.8&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The highest point in Boston is <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Hill,_Boston" title="Bellevue Hill, Boston">Bellevue Hill</a> at 330 feet (100&#160;m) above sea level, and the lowest point is at sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Situated onshore of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, Boston is the only state capital in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a> with an oceanic <a href="/wiki/Shoreline" class="mw-redirect" title="Shoreline">shoreline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The geographical center of Boston is in Roxbury. Due north of the center we find the South End. This is not to be confused with South Boston which lies directly east from the South End. North of South Boston is East Boston and southwest of East Boston is the North End.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Author, Unknown \xe2\x80\x93 A common local colloquialism</cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Boston is surrounded by the "<a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a>" region and is contiguously bordered by the <a href="/wiki/New_England_town" title="New England town">cities and towns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Winthrop,_Massachusetts" title="Winthrop, Massachusetts">Winthrop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revere,_Massachusetts" title="Revere, Massachusetts">Revere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_Massachusetts" title="Chelsea, Massachusetts">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Everett,_Massachusetts" title="Everett, Massachusetts">Everett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watertown,_Massachusetts" title="Watertown, Massachusetts">Watertown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newton,_Massachusetts" title="Newton, Massachusetts">Newton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brookline,_Massachusetts" title="Brookline, Massachusetts">Brookline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Needham,_Massachusetts" title="Needham, Massachusetts">Needham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dedham,_Massachusetts" title="Dedham, Massachusetts">Dedham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Massachusetts" title="Canton, Massachusetts">Canton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Massachusetts" title="Milton, Massachusetts">Milton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quincy,_Massachusetts" title="Quincy, Massachusetts">Quincy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a> separates Boston from <a href="/wiki/Watertown,_Massachusetts" title="Watertown, Massachusetts">Watertown</a> and the majority of Cambridge, and the mass of Boston from its own Charlestown neighborhood. To the east lie <a href="/wiki/Boston_Harbor" title="Boston Harbor">Boston Harbor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Harbor_Islands_National_Recreation_Area" title="Boston Harbor Islands National Recreation Area">Boston Harbor Islands National Recreation Area</a> (which includes part of the city\'s territory, specifically <a href="/wiki/Calf_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Calf Island (Massachusetts)">Calf Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallops_Island" title="Gallops Island">Gallops Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Brewster_Island" title="Great Brewster Island">Great Brewster Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Green Island (Massachusetts)">Green Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Brewster_Island" title="Little Brewster Island">Little Brewster Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Calf_Island" title="Little Calf Island">Little Calf Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lovells_Island" title="Lovells Island">Lovells Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Brewster_Island" title="Middle Brewster Island">Middle Brewster Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nixes_Mate" title="Nixes Mate">Nixes Mate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outer_Brewster_Island" title="Outer Brewster Island">Outer Brewster Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rainsford_Island" title="Rainsford Island">Rainsford Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shag_Rocks_(Massachusetts)" title="Shag Rocks (Massachusetts)">Shag Rocks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spectacle_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Spectacle Island (Massachusetts)">Spectacle Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Graves_(Massachusetts)" title="The Graves (Massachusetts)">The Graves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thompson_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Thompson Island (Massachusetts)">Thompson Island</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Neponset_River" title="Neponset River">Neponset River</a> forms the boundary between Boston\'s southern neighborhoods and the city of <a href="/wiki/Quincy,_Massachusetts" title="Quincy, Massachusetts">Quincy</a> and the town of <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Massachusetts" title="Milton, Massachusetts">Milton</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mystic_River" title="Mystic River">Mystic River</a> separates Charlestown from Chelsea and Everett, and Chelsea Creek and Boston Harbor separate East Boston from Boston proper.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscapes">Cityscapes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cityscapes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1808px;">\n<div class="nowrap">&#160;</span>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Neighborhoods_in_Boston" title="Neighborhoods in Boston">Neighborhoods in Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg/220px-JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg" width="220" height="447" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg/330px-JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg/440px-JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2099" data-file-height="4265" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JohnHancockTowerHDRApr09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/200_Clarendon_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="200 Clarendon Street">200 Clarendon Street</a> is the tallest building in Boston, with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world_by_height_to_roof" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tallest buildings in the world by height to roof">roof height</a> of 790 feet (240&#160;m).</div></div></div>\n<p>Boston is sometimes called a "city of neighborhoods" because of the profusion of diverse subsections; the city government\'s Office of Neighborhood Services has officially designated 23 neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> More than two-thirds of inner Boston\'s modern land area did not exist when the city was founded. Instead, it was created via the gradual filling in of the surrounding tidal areas over the centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-landfills_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landfills-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> with earth from leveling or lowering Boston\'s three original hills (the "Trimountain", after which Tremont Street is named) and with gravel brought by train from Needham to fill the <a href="/wiki/Back_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Back Bay">Back Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris20058_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris20058-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Downtown_Boston" title="Downtown Boston">Downtown</a> and its immediate surroundings consist largely of low-rise masonry buildings (often <a href="/wiki/Federal_architecture" title="Federal architecture">Federal style</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Revival">Greek Revival</a>) interspersed with modern highrises, in the Financial District, Government Center, and <a href="/wiki/South_Boston" title="South Boston">South Boston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Back Bay includes many prominent landmarks, such as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Library" title="Boston Public Library">Boston Public Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_First_Church_of_Christ,_Scientist" title="The First Church of Christ, Scientist">Christian Science Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copley_Square" title="Copley Square">Copley Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newbury_Street" title="Newbury Street">Newbury Street</a>, and New England\'s two tallest buildings: the <a href="/wiki/200_Clarendon_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="200 Clarendon Street">John Hancock Tower</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Tower" title="Prudential Tower">Prudential Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\nNear the John Hancock Tower is the <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Building" title="Berkeley Building">old John Hancock Building</a> with its prominent <a href="/wiki/Weather_beacon" title="Weather beacon">illuminated beacon</a>, the color of which forecasts the weather.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull201191_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull201191-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Smaller commercial areas are interspersed among areas of single-family homes and wooden/brick multi-family row houses. The South End Historic District is the largest surviving contiguous Victorian-era neighborhood in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The geography of downtown and South Boston was particularly affected by the Central Artery/Tunnel Project (known unofficially as the "<a href="/wiki/Big_Dig" title="Big Dig">Big Dig</a>") which removed the unsightly elevated <a href="/wiki/Central_Artery" title="Central Artery">Central Artery</a> and incorporated new green spaces and open areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris200554,_102_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris200554,_102-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right"><span style="font-size:80%">11</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:7.1622222222222em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right"><span style="font-size:80%">3</span></div>\n</div></td>\n<td><div style="width:1.6em;height:17em;position:relative;padding:0;margin:0">\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:2em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #abc;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="background:#ace;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;bottom:2em;left:.2em;width:1.2em;height:1.92024em;overflow:hidden">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:blue;position:absolute;bottom:.5em;left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:70%">96</span></div>\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="overflow:hidden;background:#e44;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;left:.2em;width:1.2em;bottom:7.5733333333333em;height:1.4444444444444em;">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:9.0177777777778em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right"><span style="font-size:80%">5</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:6.0733333333333em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right"><span style="font-size:80%">\xe2\x88\x922</span></div>\n</div></td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0C</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in mm</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg/310px-Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg" width="310" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg/465px-Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg/620px-Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1258" data-file-height="772" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Snowfall-Boston-NWS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A graph of cumulative winter snowfall at <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan International Airport</a> from 1938\xe2\x80\x932015. The four winters with the greatest amount of snowfall are highlighted. The snowfall data, which was collected by <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">NOAA</a>, is from the weather station at the airport.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>, Boston has a hot summer <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (K\xc3\xb6ppen <i>Dfa</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Summers are typically warm and humid, while winters are cold and stormy, with occasional periods of heavy snow. Spring and fall are usually cool to mild, with varying conditions dependent on wind direction and jet stream positioning. Prevailing wind patterns that blow offshore minimize the influence of the Atlantic Ocean; however, in winter areas near the immediate coast will often see more rain than snow as warm air is drawn off the Atlantic at times.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonWeather_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonWeather-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The city lies at the transition between <a href="/wiki/USDA" class="mw-redirect" title="USDA">USDA</a> plant <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zones</a> 6b (most of the city) and 7a (Downtown, South Boston, and East Boston neighborhoods).<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The hottest month is July, with a mean temperature of 73.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F (23.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C). The coldest month is January, with a mean of 29.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x921.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C). Periods exceeding 90&#160;\xc2\xb0F (32&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in summer and below freezing in winter are not uncommon but rarely extended, with about 13 and 25&#160;days per year seeing each, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The most recent sub-0&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9218&#160;\xc2\xb0C) reading occurred on January 7, 2018, when the temperature dipped down to \xe2\x88\x922&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9219&#160;\xc2\xb0C).<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In addition, several decades may pass between 100&#160;\xc2\xb0F (38&#160;\xc2\xb0C) readings, with the most recent such occurrence on July 22, 2011, when the temperature reached 103&#160;\xc2\xb0F (39&#160;\xc2\xb0C).<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s average window for freezing temperatures is November 9 through April 5.<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> Official temperature records have ranged from \xe2\x88\x9218&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9228&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on February 9, 1934, up to 104&#160;\xc2\xb0F (40&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on July 4, 1911; the record cold daily maximum is 2&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9217&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on December 30, 1917, while, conversely, the record warm daily minimum is 83&#160;\xc2\xb0F (28&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on August 2, 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston\'s coastal location on the North Atlantic moderates its temperature but makes the city very prone to <a href="/wiki/Nor%27easter" title="Nor&#39;easter">Nor\'easter</a> weather systems that can produce much snow and rain.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonWeather_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonWeather-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The city averages 43.8 inches (1,110&#160;mm) of <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> a year, with 43.8 inches (111&#160;cm) of snowfall per season.<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Snowfall increases dramatically as one goes inland away from the city (especially north and west of the city)\xe2\x80\x94away from the moderating influence of the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Most snowfall occurs from mid-November through early April, and snow is rare in May and October.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> There is also high year-to-year variability in snowfall; for instance, the winter of 2011\xe2\x80\x9312 saw only 9.3&#160;in (23.6&#160;cm) of accumulating snow, but the previous winter, the corresponding figure was 81.0&#160;in (2.06&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)_100-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWS_Boston,_MA_(BOX)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Autumn foliage with a city skyline in the distant background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg/220px-USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg/330px-USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg/440px-USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="407" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USA_Massachusetts_Boston_Foliage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boston\'s skyline in the background, with <a href="/wiki/Autumn_leaf_color" title="Autumn leaf color">fall foliage</a> in the foreground</div></div></div>\n<p>Fog is fairly common, particularly in spring and early summer. Due to its situation along the North Atlantic, the city often receives sea breezes, especially in the late spring, when water temperatures are still quite cold and temperatures at the coast can be more than 20&#160;\xc2\xb0F (11&#160;\xc2\xb0C) colder than a few miles inland, sometimes dropping by that amount near midday.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\nThunderstorms occur from May to September, that are occasionally severe with large <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a>, damaging winds and heavy downpours.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonWeather_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonWeather-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Although downtown Boston has never been struck by a violent <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a>, the city itself has experienced many <a href="/wiki/Tornado_warning" title="Tornado warning">tornado warnings</a>. Damaging storms are more common to areas north, west, and northwest of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Boston has a relatively sunny climate for a coastal city at its latitude, averaging over 2,300 hours of sunshine per annum.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed"
