href="#cite_note-1950_Census_Urban_populations_since_1790-125">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><br />Source: <center>U.S. Decennial Census<sup id="cite_ref-DecennialCensus_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DecennialCensus-127">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></center></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 2016, Boston was estimated to have 673,184 residents (a density of 13,841 persons/sq mi, or 5,344/km<sup>2</sup>) living in 272,481 housing units<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94a 9% population increase over 2010. The city is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population_density" title="List of United States cities by population density">third-most densely populated large U.S. city</a> of over half a million residents. Some 1.2&#160;million persons may be within Boston\'s boundaries during work hours, and as many as 2&#160;million during special events. This fluctuation of people is caused by hundreds of thousands of suburban residents who travel to the city for work, education, health care, and special events.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the city, the population was spread out with 21.9% at age 19 and under, 14.3% from 20 to 24, 33.2% from 25 to 44, 20.4% from 45 to 64, and 10.1% who were 65&#160;years of age or older. The median age was 30.8&#160;years. For every 100 females, there were 92.0 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 89.9 males.<sup id="cite_ref-census1_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-129">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> There were 252,699 households, of which 20.4% had children under the age of 18 living in them, 25.5% were married couples living together, 16.3% had a female householder with no husband present, and 54.0% were non-families. 37.1% of all households were made up of individuals and 9.0% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.26 and the average family size was 3.08.<sup id="cite_ref-census1_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-129">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Boston has one of the <a href="/wiki/LGBT_demographics_of_the_United_States#By_city" title="LGBT demographics of the United States">largest LGBT populations in the United States</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Median_income" title="Median income">median household income</a> in Boston was $51,739, while the median income for a family was $61,035. Full-time year-round male workers had a median income of $52,544 versus $46,540 for full-time year-round female workers. The per capita income for the city was $33,158. 21.4% of the population and 16.0% of families are below the poverty line. Of the total population, 28.8% of those under the age of 18 and 20.4% of those 65 and older were living below the poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-census3_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census3-130">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1950, <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">Whites</a> represented 94.7% of Boston\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-census4_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census4-131">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> From the 1950s to the end of the 20th century, the proportion of <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">non-Hispanic whites</a> in the city declined; in 2000, non-Hispanic whites made up 49.5% of the city\'s population, making the city <a href="/wiki/Majority_minority" title="Majority minority">majority minority</a> for the first time. However, in the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a>, the city has experienced significant <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>, in which affluent whites have moved into formerly non-white areas. In 2006, the US Census Bureau estimated that non-Hispanic whites again formed a slight majority. But as of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, in part due to the housing crash, as well as increased efforts to make more affordable housing more available, the non-white population has rebounded. This may also have to do with increased <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">Asian</a> populations and more clarity surrounding US Census statistics, which indicate a non-Hispanic white population of 47 percent (some reports give slightly lower figures).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Race/ethnicity composition\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Race/ethnicity</th>\n<th>2015<sup id="cite_ref-135" Boston">Chinatown</a>, with its <a href="/wiki/Paifang" title="Paifang">paifang</a> gate, is home to many <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Chinese Americans in Boston">Chinese</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Vietnamese Americans in Boston">Vietnamese</a> restaurants.</div></div></div>\n<p>People of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Irish_Americans_in_Boston" title="History of Irish Americans in Boston">Irish</a> descent form the largest single <a href="/wiki/American_ancestry" title="American ancestry">ethnic group</a> in the city, making up 15.8% of the population, followed by <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">Italians</a>, accounting for 8.3% of the population. People of <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> ancestry are another sizable group, at 6.0%,<sup id="cite_ref-census2_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2-137">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> about half of whom are of <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Americans" title="Haitian Americans">Haitian</a> ancestry. Over 27,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Chinese Americans in Boston">Chinese Americans</a> made their home in Boston city proper in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and the city hosts a growing <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Boston" title="Chinatown, Boston">Chinatown</a> accommodating heavily traveled <a href="/wiki/Chinatown_bus_lines" title="Chinatown bus lines">Chinese-owned bus lines</a> to and from <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown, Manhattan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_in_New_York_City" title="Chinese in New York City">New York City</a>. Some neighborhoods, such as Dorchester, have received an influx of people of <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Vietnamese Americans in Boston">Vietnamese</a> ancestry in recent decades. Neighborhoods such as Jamaica Plain and Roslindale have experienced a growing number of <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans" title="Dominican Americans">Dominican Americans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The city and greater area also has a growing immigrant population of <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_ethnic_groups" title="South Asian ethnic groups">South Asians</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Americans#US_Metropolitan_areas_with_the_largest_population_of_Indian_Americans" title="Indian Americans">tenth-largest Indian population in the country</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_(5559894531).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png/220px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png/330px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png/440px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_%285559894531%29.png 2x" data-file-width="3009" data-file-height="3009" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Boston_(5559894531).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of racial distribution in Boston, 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people: <span style="color:#ff0000"><b>White</b></span>, <span style="color:#0000ff"><b>Black</b></span>, <span style="color:#00ff80"><b>Asian</b></span>, <span style="color:#ff8000"><b>Hispanic</b></span>, or <b>Other</b> (yellow)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/220px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/330px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/440px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boston <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">gay pride</a> march, held annually in June</div></div></div>\n<p>The city, especially the <a href="/wiki/East_Boston" title="East Boston">East Boston</a> neighborhood, has a significant Hispanic population. In 2010, Hispanics in Boston were mostly of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">Puerto Rican</a> (30,506 or 4.9% of total city population), <a href="/wiki/Dominican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominican American">Dominican</a> (25,648 or 4.2% of total city population), <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Americans" title="Salvadoran Americans">Salvadoran</a> (10,850 or 1.8% of city population), <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Americans" title="Colombian Americans">Colombian</a> (6,649 or 1.1% of total city population), <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Americans" title="Mexican Americans">Mexican</a> (5,961 or 1.0% of total city population), and <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_Americans" title="Guatemalan Americans">Guatemalan</a> (4,451 or 0.7% of total city population) ethnic origin. Hispanics of all national origins totaled 107,917 in 2010. In Greater Boston, these numbers grew significantly, with Puerto Ricans numbering 175,000+, Dominicans 95,000+, Salvadorans 40,000+, Guatemalans 31,000+, Mexicans 25,000+, and Colombians numbering 22,000+.<sup id="cite_ref-census_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-140">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG/220px-OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG/330px-OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG/440px-OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1481" data-file-height="1971" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OldSouthChurchBoston.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Old_South_Church" title="Old South Church">Old South Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Christ" title="United Church of Christ">United Church of Christ</a> congregation first organized in 1669</div></div></div>\n<p>According to a 2014 study by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 57% of the population of the city identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a>, with 25% professing attendance at a variety of churches that could be considered <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>, and 29% professing <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> while 33% claim <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religious affiliation</a>. The same study says that other religions (including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>) collectively make up about 10% of the population.\n</p><p>As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the Catholic Church had the highest number of adherents as a single denomination in the Boston-Cambridge-Newton Metro area, with more than two million members and 339 churches, followed by the Episcopal Church with 58,000 adherents in 160 churches. The <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Christ" title="United Church of Christ">United Church of Christ</a> had 55,000 members and 213 churches.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The UCC is the successor of the city\'s Puritan religious traditions. <a href="/wiki/Old_South_Church" title="Old South Church">Old South Church</a> in Boston is one of the oldest congregations in the United States. It was organized in 1669 by dissenters from the First Church in Boston (1630). Past members include Samuel Adams, William Dawes, Benjamin Franklin, Samuel Sewall, and Phillis Wheatley. In 1773, Adams gave the signals from the <a href="/wiki/Old_South_Meeting_House" title="Old South Meeting House">Old South Meeting House</a> that started the Boston Tea Party.\n</p><p>The city has a <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">Jewish population</a> with an estimated 248,000 Jews within the Boston metro area.<sup id="cite_ref-2015bjcs_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015bjcs-147">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> More than half of Jewish households in the Greater Boston area reside in the city itself, Brookline, Newton, Cambridge, Somerville, or adjacent towns.<sup id="cite_ref-2015bjcs_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015bjcs-147">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston#Major_companies" title="Greater Boston">Major companies in Greater Boston</a></div>\n<table class="toc" style="float:left; font-size:90%; text-align:center; margin:1em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="7" style="background:tan;"><b>Top publicly area">NECTA</a> Labor Force</b> (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Finance &amp; real estate (8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Professional &amp; business services (15%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Educational &amp; health services (28%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f3d827; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Leisure &amp; hospitality (9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a3c409; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other services (4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #c31074; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Government (4%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>, Boston is placed among the top 30 most economically powerful cities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Encompassing $363&#160;billion, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a> metropolitan area has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">sixth-largest economy in the country and 12th-largest in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pricewater_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pricewater-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston\'s colleges and universities exert a significant impact on the regional economy. Boston attracts more than 350,000 college students from around the world, who contribute more than US$4.8&#160;billion annually to the city\'s economy.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The area\'s schools are major employers and attract industries to the city and surrounding region. The city is home to a number of technology companies and is a hub for <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Milken_Institute" title="Milken Institute">Milken Institute</a> rating Boston as the top <a href="/wiki/List_of_life_sciences" title="List of life sciences">life sciences</a> cluster in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Boston receives the highest absolute amount of annual funding from the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> of all cities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is considered highly innovative for a variety of reasons, including the presence of <a href="/wiki/Academia" class="mw-redirect" title="Academia">academia</a>, access to <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a>, and the presence of many <a href="/wiki/High-tech" class="mw-redirect" title="High-tech">high-tech</a> companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Kirsner_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirsner-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_128" title="Massachusetts Route 128">Route 128 corridor</a> and Greater Boston continue to be a major center for venture capital investment,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and high technology remains an important sector.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> also composes a large part of Boston\'s economy, with 21.2 million domestic and international visitors spending $8.3&#160;billion in 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> excluding visitors from <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, over 1.4 million international tourists visited Boston in 2014, with those from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> leading the list.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s status as a state capital as well as the regional home of federal agencies has rendered law and government to be another major component of the city\'s economy.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The city is a major <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Boston" title="Port of Boston">seaport</a> along the East Coast of the United States and the oldest continuously operated industrial and fishing port in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> industry is important to Boston, especially involving <a href="/wiki/Mutual_fund" title="Mutual fund">mutual funds</a> and insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a>, Boston was ranked as having the ninth-most competitive financial center in the world and the fourth-most competitive in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Boston-based <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_Investments" title="Fidelity Investments">Fidelity Investments</a> helped popularize the mutual fund in the 1980s and has made Boston one of the top financial centers in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The city is home to the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bank" title="Santander Bank">Santander Bank</a>, and Boston is a center for <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> firms. <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Corporation" title="State Street Corporation">State Street Corporation</a>, which specializes in asset management and custody services, is based in the city. Boston is a printing and <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">publishing</a> center<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Houghton_Mifflin_Harcourt" title="Houghton Mifflin Harcourt">Houghton Mifflin Harcourt</a> is headquartered within the city, along with <a href="/wiki/Bedford-St._Martin%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedford-St. Martin&#39;s">Bedford-St. Martin\'s Press</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Press" title="Beacon Press">Beacon Press</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pearson_PLC" class="mw-redirect" title="Pearson PLC">Pearson PLC</a> publishing units also employ several hundred people in Boston. The city is home to three major <a href="/wiki/Convention_center" title="Convention center">convention centers</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Hynes_Convention_Center" title="Hynes Convention Center">Hynes Convention Center</a> in the Back Bay, and the <a href="/wiki/Seaport_Hotel_and_Seaport_World_Trade_Center" title="Seaport Hotel and Seaport World Trade Center">Seaport World Trade Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Convention_and_Exhibition_Center" title="Boston Convention and Exhibition Center">Boston Convention and Exhibition Center</a> on the <a href="/wiki/South_Boston_waterfront" class="mw-redirect" title="South Boston waterfront">South Boston waterfront</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="General Electric Corporation">General Electric Corporation</a> announced in January 2016 its decision to move the company\'s global headquarters to the <a href="/wiki/Seaport_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport District">Seaport District</a> in Boston, from <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield, Connecticut">Fairfield, Connecticut</a>, citing factors including Boston\'s preeminence in the realm of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Boston is home to the headquarters of several major athletic and footwear companies including <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Balance" title="New Balance">New Balance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rockport_(company)" title="Rockport (company)">Rockport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puma_(brand)" title="Puma (brand)">Puma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolverine_World_Wide" title="Wolverine World Wide">Wolverine World Wide, Inc.</a> headquarters or regional offices<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> are located just outside the city.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Three-story brick building fa\xc3\xa7ade with three white columns surrounding a brown wooden door located on the ground floor" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg/220px-Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg/330px-Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg/440px-Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1214" data-file-height="757" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Latin_School_-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_School" title="Boston Latin School">Boston Latin School</a> was established in 1635 and is the oldest public high school in the US.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Schools" title="Boston Public Schools">Boston Public Schools</a> enroll 57,000 students attending 145 schools, including the renowned <a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_Academy" title="Boston Latin Academy">Boston Latin Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_D._O%27Bryant_School_of_Mathematics_%26_Science" title="John D. O&#39;Bryant School of Mathematics &amp; Science">John D. O\'Bryant School of Math &amp; Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Latin_School" title="Boston Latin School">Boston Latin School</a>. The Boston Latin School was established in 1635 and is the oldest public high school in the US. Boston also operates the United States\' second-oldest public high school and its oldest public elementary school.<sup id="cite_ref-BPS_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The system\'s students are 40% Hispanic or Latino, 35% Black or African American, 13% White, and 9% Asian.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> There are private, parochial, and <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter schools</a> as well, and approximately 3,300 minority students attend participating suburban schools through the <a href="/wiki/METCO" title="METCO">Metropolitan Educational Opportunity Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Boston" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston">List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_college_town_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Boston_college_town_map.png/220px-Boston_college_town_map.png" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Boston_college_town_map.png/330px-Boston_college_town_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Boston_college_town_map.png/440px-Boston_college_town_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2213" data-file-height="2010" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_college_town_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Boston-area universities</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome,_Cambridge_MA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="MIT Building 10 and the Great Dome, Cambridge Massachusetts" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/220px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/330px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/440px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome,_Cambridge_MA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT) is often cited as among the world\'s top universities.</div></div></div>\n<p>Some of the most renowned and highly ranked universities in the world are located near Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Three universities with a major presence in the city, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts</a>, are located just outside of Boston in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville</a>, known as the <i>Brainpower Triangle</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Harvard is the nation\'s oldest institute of higher education and is centered across the Charles River in Cambridge, though the majority of its land holdings and a substantial amount of its educational activities are in Boston. Its <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School" title="Harvard Medical School">medical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="Harvard School of Dental Medicine">dental</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_School_of_Public_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard School of Public Health">public health</a> schools are located in Boston\'s <a href="/wiki/Allston" title="Allston">Allston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longwood_Medical_and_Academic_Area" title="Longwood Medical and Academic Area">Longwood</a> neighborhoods, and Harvard has plans for additional expansion into Allston.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT) originated in Boston and was long known as "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology#Boston_Tech_(1865\xe2\x80\x931916)" title="History of the Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Boston Tech</a>"; it moved across the river to Cambridge in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts University</a>\'s main campus is north of the city in <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medford,_Massachusetts" title="Medford, Massachusetts">Medford</a>, though it locates its medical and dental schools in Boston\'s Chinatown at <a href="/wiki/Tufts_Medical_Center" title="Tufts Medical Center">Tufts Medical Center</a>, a 451-bed academic medical institution that is home to both a full-service hospital for adults and the Floating Hospital for Children.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Four members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> are in Greater Boston (more than any other metropolitan area): <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brandeis_University" title="Brandeis University">Brandeis University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, Greater Boston contains seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_research_universities_in_the_United_States#Universities_classified_as_&quot;R1:_Doctoral_Universities_\xe2\x80\x93_Highest_Research_Activity&quot;" title="List of research universities in the United States">Highest Research Activity (R1) Universities</a> as per the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification</a>. This includes, in addition to the aforementioned four, <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts University</a>. This is, by a large margin, the highest concentration of such institutions in a single metropolitan area.\nHospitals, universities, and research institutions in Greater Boston received more than $1.77 billion in <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> grants in 2013, more money than any other American metropolitan area.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greater Boston has more than 100 colleges and universities, with 250,000 students enrolled in Boston and Cambridge alone.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s largest private universities include <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a> (also the city\'s fourth-largest employer),<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> with its main campus along <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Avenue_(Boston)" title="Commonwealth Avenue (Boston)">Commonwealth Avenue</a> and a medical campus in the <a href="/wiki/South_End,_Boston" title="South End, Boston">South End</a>; <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Fenway%E2%80%93Kenmore" title="Fenway\xe2\x80\x93Kenmore">Fenway</a> area;<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_University" title="Suffolk University">Suffolk University</a> near <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Hill,_Boston" title="Beacon Hill, Boston">Beacon Hill</a>, which includes <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_University_Law_School" title="Suffolk University Law School">law school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sawyer_Business_School" title="Sawyer Business School">business school</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, which straddles the Boston (Brighton)\xe2\x80\x93Newton border.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s only public university is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Boston" title="University of Massachusetts Boston">University of Massachusetts Boston</a> on Columbia Point in <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorchester, Massachusetts">Dorchester</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roxbury_Community_College" title="Roxbury Community College">Roxbury Community College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bunker_Hill_Community_College" title="Bunker Hill Community College">Bunker Hill Community College</a> are the city\'s two public community colleges. Altogether, Boston\'s colleges and universities employ more than 42,600 people, accounting for nearly seven percent of the city\'s workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG/220px-Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG/330px-Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG/440px-Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_business_school_baker_library_2009a.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a>, one of the country\'s top <a href="/wiki/Business_school" title="Business school">business schools</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Smaller private colleges include <a href="/wiki/Babson_College" title="Babson College">Babson College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bentley_University" title="Bentley University">Bentley University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Architectural_College" title="Boston Architectural College">Boston Architectural College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_College_(Massachusetts)" title="Emmanuel College (Massachusetts)">Emmanuel College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fisher_College" title="Fisher College">Fisher College</a>, <a href="/wiki/MGH_Institute_of_Health_Professions" title="MGH Institute of Health Professions">MGH Institute of Health Professions</a>, <a href="/wiki/MCPHS_University" title="MCPHS University">Massachusetts College of Pharmacy and Health Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simmons_College" title="Simmons College">Simmons College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wellesley_College" title="Wellesley College">Wellesley College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheelock_College" title="Wheelock College">Wheelock College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wentworth_Institute_of_Technology" title="Wentworth Institute of Technology">Wentworth Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_England_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="New England School of Law">New England School of Law</a> (originally established as America\'s first all female law school),<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Emerson_College" title="Emerson College">Emerson College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Metropolitan Boston is home to several <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatories</a> and art schools, including <a href="/wiki/Lesley_University" title="Lesley University">Lesley University College of Art and Design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_College_of_Art_and_Design" title="Massachusetts College of Art and Design">Massachusetts College of Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_the_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_at_Tufts" title="School of the Museum of Fine Arts at Tufts">School of the Museum of Fine Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_England_Institute_of_Art" title="New England Institute of Art">New England Institute of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_England_School_of_Art_and_Design" title="New England School of Art and Design">New England School of Art and Design</a> (Suffolk University), <a href="/wiki/Longy_School_of_Music_of_Bard_College" title="Longy School of Music of Bard College">Longy School of Music of Bard College</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Conservatory_of_Music" title="New England Conservatory of Music">New England Conservatory</a> (the oldest independent conservatory in the United States).<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Other conservatories include the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Conservatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Conservatory">Boston Conservatory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music" title="Berklee College of Music">Berklee College of Music</a>, which has made Boston an important city for jazz music.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_safety">Public safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="White Boston Police car with blue and gray stripes down the middle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg/220px-Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg/330px-Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg/440px-Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2052" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Police_cruiser_on_Beacon_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Boston Police cruiser on Beacon Street</div></div></div>\n<p>Like many major American cities, Boston has seen a great reduction in violent crime since the early 1990s. Boston\'s low crime rate since the 1990s has been credited to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Police_Department" title="Boston Police Department">Boston Police Department</a>\'s collaboration with neighborhood groups and church parishes to prevent youths from joining gangs, as well as involvement from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney" title="United States Attorney">United States Attorney and District Attorney</a>\'s offices. This helped lead in part to what has been touted as the "Boston Miracle". Murders in the city dropped from 152 in 1990 (for a murder rate of 26.5 per 100,000 people) to just 31\xe2\x80\x94not one of them a juvenile\xe2\x80\x94in 1999 (for a murder rate of 5.26 per 100,000).<sup id="cite_ref-End_of_a_Miracle_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-End_of_a_Miracle-191">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, there were 62 reported homicides.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonCrimeStats_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonCrimeStats-192">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Through December 30, 2016, major crime was down seven percent and there were 46 homicides compared to 40 in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_in_Boston" title="Culture in Boston">Culture in Boston</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_annual_events_in_Boston" title="List of annual events in Boston">List of annual events in Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_arts_organizations_in_Boston" title="List of arts organizations in Boston">List of arts organizations in Boston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sites_of_interest_in_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Sites of interest in Boston">Sites of interest in Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colonial style red brick building with a white cupola in an urban setting" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg/170px-Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg" width="170" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg/255px-Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg/340px-Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2403" data-file-height="1892" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_State_House_Boston_Massachusetts2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_State_House_(Boston)" title="Old State House (Boston)">Old State House</a>, a museum on the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Trail" title="Freedom Trail">Freedom Trail</a> and the site of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Massacre" title="Boston Massacre">Boston Massacre</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg/220px-2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg/330px-2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg/440px-2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3475" data-file-height="2317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2009_HanoverSt_Boston.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hanover_Street_(Boston)" title="Hanover Street (Boston)">Hanover Street</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_End,_Boston" title="North End, Boston">North End</a> is known for its restaurants.</div></div></div>\n<p>Boston shares many cultural roots with greater New England, including a dialect of the non-<a href="/wiki/Rhoticity_in_English" title="Rhoticity in English">rhotic</a> Eastern <a href="/wiki/New_England_English" title="New England English">New England accent</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_accent" title="Boston accent">Boston accent</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVorhees200952_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVorhees200952-194">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/New_England_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="New England cuisine">regional cuisine</a> with a large emphasis on seafood, salt, and dairy products.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVorhees2009148\xe2\x80\x93151_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVorhees2009148\xe2\x80\x93151-195">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Boston also has its own collection of <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">neologisms</a> known as <i>Boston slang</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OldCornerBookstore08.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/OldCornerBookstore08.JPG/220px-OldCornerBookstore08.JPG" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/OldCornerBookstore08.JPG/330px-OldCornerBookstore08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/OldCornerBookstore08.JPG/440px-OldCornerBookstore08.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2621" data-file-height="2382" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OldCornerBookstore08.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the nineteenth century, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Corner_Bookstore" title="Old Corner Bookstore">Old Corner Bookstore</a> became a gathering place for writers, including <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Emerson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Thoreau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Fuller" title="Margaret Fuller">Margaret Fuller</a>. Here <a href="/wiki/James_Russell_Lowell" title="James Russell Lowell">James Russell Lowell</a> printed the first editions of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic_Monthly" class="mw-redirect" title="The Atlantic Monthly">The Atlantic Monthly</a></i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the early 1800s, <a href="/wiki/William_Tudor_(1779%E2%80%931830)" title="William Tudor (1779\xe2\x80\x931830)">William Tudor</a> wrote that Boston was "\'perhaps the most perfect and certainly the best-regulated democracy that ever existed. There is something so impossible in the immortal fame of Athens, that the very name makes everything modern shrink from comparison; but since the days of that glorious city I know of none that has approached so near in some points, distant as it may still be from that illustrious model.\'<sup id="cite_ref-Vennochi_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vennochi-197">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> From this, Boston has been called the "<a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> of America" (also a nickname of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>) for its <a href="/wiki/Literary_genre" title="Literary genre">literary culture</a>, earning a reputation as "the intellectual capital of the United States."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-199">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the nineteenth century, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Hawthorne" title="Nathaniel Hawthorne">Nathaniel Hawthorne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Fuller" title="Margaret Fuller">Margaret Fuller</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Russell_Lowell" title="James Russell Lowell">James Russell Lowell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Henry Wadsworth Longfellow</a> wrote in Boston. Some consider the <a href="/wiki/Old_Corner_Bookstore" title="Old Corner Bookstore">Old Corner Bookstore</a> to be the "cradle of American literature," the place where these writers met and where <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic_Monthly" class="mw-redirect" title="The Atlantic Monthly">The Atlantic Monthly</a></i> was first published.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> In 1852, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Library" title="Boston Public Library">Boston Public Library</a> was founded as the first free library in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-199">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s literary culture continues today thanks to the city\'s many universities and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Book_Festival" title="Boston Book Festival">Boston Book Festival</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_symphony_hall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Boston_symphony_hall.JPG/220px-Boston_symphony_hall.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Boston_symphony_hall.JPG/330px-Boston_symphony_hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Boston_symphony_hall.JPG/440px-Boston_symphony_hall.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_symphony_hall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Symphony_Hall,_Boston" title="Symphony Hall, Boston">Symphony Hall</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Boston Symphony Orchestra">Boston Symphony Orchestra</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordanhallbalcony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jordanhallbalcony.jpg/220px-Jordanhallbalcony.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jordanhallbalcony.jpg/330px-Jordanhallbalcony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jordanhallbalcony.jpg/440px-Jordanhallbalcony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordanhallbalcony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jordan_Hall" title="Jordan Hall">Jordan Hall</a> at the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Conservatory" class="mw-redirect" title="New England Conservatory">New England Conservatory</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Music is afforded a high degree of <a href="/wiki/Civic_engagement" title="Civic engagement">civic support</a> in Boston. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Boston Symphony Orchestra">Boston Symphony Orchestra</a> is one of the "<a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(orchestras)" title="Big Five (orchestras)">Big Five</a>," a group of the greatest American orchestras, and the classical music magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Gramophone_(magazine)" title="Gramophone (magazine)">Gramophone</a></i> called it one of the "world\'s best" orchestras.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Hall,_Boston" title="Symphony Hall, Boston">Symphony Hall</a> (located west of Back Bay) is home to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Boston Symphony Orchestra">Boston Symphony Orchestra</a> and the related <a href="/wiki/Boston_Youth_Symphony_Orchestras" title="Boston Youth Symphony Orchestras">Boston Youth Symphony Orchestra</a>, which is the largest youth orchestra in the nation, and to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Pops_Orchestra" title="Boston Pops Orchestra">Boston Pops Orchestra</a>. The British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> called Boston Symphony Hall "one of the top venues for classical music in the world," adding that "Symphony Hall in Boston was where science became an essential part of concert hall design."<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Other concerts are held at the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Conservatory_of_Music" title="New England Conservatory of Music">New England Conservatory</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Hall" title="Jordan Hall">Jordan Hall</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Ballet" title="Boston Ballet">Boston Ballet</a> performs at the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Opera_House_(1980)" title="Boston Opera House (1980)">Boston Opera House</a>. Other performing-arts organizations located in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Lyric_Opera" title="Boston Lyric Opera">Boston Lyric Opera Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera_Boston" title="Opera Boston">Opera Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Baroque" title="Boston Baroque">Boston Baroque</a> (the first permanent Baroque orchestra in the US),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull2011175_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull2011175-203">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Handel_and_Haydn_Society" title="Handel and Haydn Society">Handel and Haydn Society</a> (one of the oldest choral companies in the United States).<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The city is a center for contemporary classical music with a number of performing groups, several of which are associated with the city\'s conservatories and universities. These include the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Modern_Orchestra_Project" title="Boston Modern Orchestra Project">Boston Modern Orchestra Project</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Musica_Viva" title="Boston Musica Viva">Boston Musica Viva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull2011175_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull2011175-203">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Several theaters are located in or near the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Street_Theatre_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Street Theatre District">Theater District</a> south of Boston Common, including the <a href="/wiki/Cutler_Majestic_Theatre" title="Cutler Majestic Theatre">Cutler Majestic Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citi_Performing_Arts_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Citi Performing Arts Center">Citi Performing Arts Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Theatre_(Boston)" title="Colonial Theatre (Boston)">Colonial Theater</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Orpheum_Theatre_(Boston)" title="Orpheum Theatre (Boston)">Orpheum Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull201153\xe2\x80\x9355_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull201153\xe2\x80\x9355-205">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are several major annual events, such as <a href="/wiki/First_Night" title="First Night">First Night</a> which occurs on New Year\'s Eve, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Early_Music_Festival" title="Boston Early Music Festival">Boston Early Music Festival</a>, the annual <a href="/wiki/Boston_Arts_Festival" title="Boston Arts Festival">Boston Arts Festival</a> at Christopher Columbus Waterfront Park, the annual Boston <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">gay pride</a> parade and festival held in June, and Italian summer feasts in the North End honoring Catholic saints.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull2011207_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull2011207-206">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The city is the site of several events during the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">Fourth of July</a> period. They include the week-long Harborfest festivities<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and a Boston Pops concert accompanied by fireworks on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mfa_boston_af.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Gray stone classical building with columns and art banners on the central fa\xc3\xa7ade" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Mfa_boston_af.jpg/220px-Mfa_boston_af.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Mfa_boston_af.jpg/330px-Mfa_boston_af.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Mfa_boston_af.jpg/440px-Mfa_boston_af.jpg 2x" data-file-width="513" data-file-height="379" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mfa_boston_af.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts,_Boston" title="Museum of Fine Arts, Boston">Museum of Fine Arts</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Several historic sites relating to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> period are preserved as part of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_National_Historical_Park" title="Boston National Historical Park">Boston National Historical Park</a> because of the city\'s prominent role. Many are found along the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Trail" title="Freedom Trail">Freedom Trail</a>, which is marked by a red line of bricks embedded in the ground.\n</p><p>The city is also home to several art museums and galleries, including the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts,_Boston" title="Museum of Fine Arts, Boston">Museum of Fine Arts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isabella_Stewart_Gardner_Museum" title="Isabella Stewart Gardner Museum">Isabella Stewart Gardner Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull2011104\xe2\x80\x93108_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull2011104\xe2\x80\x93108-209">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Contemporary_Art,_Boston" title="Institute of Contemporary Art, Boston">Institute of Contemporary Art</a> is housed in a contemporary building designed by <a href="/wiki/Diller_Scofidio_%2B_Renfro" title="Diller Scofidio + Renfro">Diller Scofidio + Renfro</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Seaport_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport District">Seaport District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s South End Art and Design District (<a href="/wiki/SoWa" title="SoWa">SoWa</a>) and Newbury St. are both art gallery destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Columbia Point is the location of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Boston" title="University of Massachusetts Boston">University of Massachusetts Boston</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Edward_M._Kennedy_Institute_for_the_United_States_Senate" title="Edward M. Kennedy Institute for the United States Senate">Edward M. Kennedy Institute for the United States Senate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Presidential_Library_and_Museum" title="John F. Kennedy Presidential Library and Museum">John F. Kennedy Presidential Library and Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Archives" title="Massachusetts Archives">Massachusetts Archives and Commonwealth Museum</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Athen%C3%A6um" title="Boston Athen\xc3\xa6um">Boston Athen\xc3\xa6um</a> (one of the oldest independent libraries in the United States),<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boston_Children%27s_Museum" title="Boston Children&#39;s Museum">Boston Children\'s Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bull_%26_Finch_Pub" class="mw-redirect" title="Bull &amp; Finch Pub">Bull &amp; Finch Pub</a> (whose building is known from the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Cheers" title="Cheers">Cheers</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull2011164_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull2011164-214">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Science_(Boston)" title="Museum of Science (Boston)">Museum of Science</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Aquarium" title="New England Aquarium">New England Aquarium</a> are within the city.\n</p><p>Boston has been a noted religious center from its earliest days. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Boston" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Boston">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Boston</a> serves nearly 300 parishes and is based in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Cross_(Boston)" title="Cathedral of the Holy Cross (Boston)">Cathedral of the Holy Cross</a> (1875) in the South End, while the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Massachusetts" title="Episcopal Diocese of Massachusetts">Episcopal Diocese of Massachusetts</a> serves just under 200 congregations, with the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Church_of_St._Paul,_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral Church of St. Paul, Boston">Cathedral Church of St. Paul</a> (1819) as its episcopal seat. <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalist_Association" title="Unitarian Universalist Association">Unitarian Universalism</a> has its headquarters on Beacon Hill. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ,_Scientist" title="Church of Christ, Scientist">Christian Scientists</a> are headquartered in Back Bay at the <a href="/wiki/The_First_Church_of_Christ,_Scientist" title="The First Church of Christ, Scientist">Mother Church</a> (1894). The oldest church in Boston is <a href="/wiki/First_Church_in_Boston" title="First Church in Boston">First Church in Boston</a>, founded in 1630.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Chapel" title="King&#39;s Chapel">King\'s Chapel</a> was the city\'s first Anglican church, founded in 1686 and converted to Unitarianism in 1785. Other churches include Christ Church (better known as <a href="/wiki/Old_North_Church" title="Old North Church">Old North Church</a>, 1723), the oldest church building in the city, <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Church,_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Church, Boston">Trinity Church</a> (1733), <a href="/wiki/Park_Street_Church" title="Park Street Church">Park Street Church</a> (1809), <a href="/wiki/Old_South_Church" title="Old South Church">Old South Church</a> (1874), <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Christian_Church" title="Jubilee Christian Church">Jubilee Christian Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Basilica_and_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Perpetual_Help" title="Basilica and Shrine of Our Lady of Perpetual Help">Basilica and Shrine of Our Lady of Perpetual Help</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mission_Hill,_Boston" title="Mission Hill, Boston">Mission Hill</a> (1878).<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_control">Pollution control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Pollution control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Air_quality" class="mw-redirect" title="Air quality">Air quality</a> in Boston is generally very good. Between 2004\xe2\x80\x932013, there were only four days in which the air was unhealthy for the general public, according to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EPA_AirCompare_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPA_AirCompare-217">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the cleaner energy facilities in Boston include the Allston green district, with three ecologically compatible housing facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Boston is also breaking ground on multiple <a href="/wiki/Green_affordable_housing" title="Green affordable housing">green affordable housing</a> facilities to help reduce the carbon impact of the city while simultaneously making these initiatives financially available to a greater population. Boston\'s climate plan is updated every three years and was most recently modified in 2013. This legislature includes the Building Energy Reporting and Disclosure Ordinance, which requires the city\'s larger buildings to disclose their yearly energy and water use statistics and to partake in an energy assessment every five years. These statistics are made public by the city, thereby increasing incentives for buildings to be more environmentally conscious.<sup id="cite_ref-scorecard.goodguide.com_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scorecard.goodguide.com-219">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mayor Thomas Menino introduced the Renew Boston Whole Building Incentive which reduces the cost of living in buildings that are deemed energy efficient. This gives people an opportunity to find housing in neighborhoods that support the environment. The ultimate goal of this initiative is to enlist 500 Bostonians to participate in a free, in-home energy assessment.<sup id="cite_ref-scorecard.goodguide.com_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scorecard.goodguide.com-219">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_purity_and_availability">Water purity and availability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Water purity and availability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Many older buildings in certain areas of Boston are supported by wooden piles driven into the area\'s fill; these piles remain sound if submerged in water, but are subject to <a href="/wiki/Dry_rot" title="Dry rot">dry rot</a> if exposed to air for long periods.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\nGround water levels have been dropping in many areas of the city, due in part to an increase in the amount of rainwater discharged directly into sewers rather than absorbed by the ground. The Boston Groundwater Trust coordinates monitoring ground water levels throughout the city via a network of public and private monitoring wells.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> However, Boston\'s drinking water supply from the <a href="/wiki/Quabbin_Reservoir" title="Quabbin Reservoir">Quabbin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wachusett_Reservoir" title="Wachusett Reservoir">Wachusett Reservoirs</a><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> is one of the very few in the country so pure as to satisfy the Federal <a href="/wiki/Clean_Water_Act" title="Clean Water Act">Clean Water Act</a> without filtration.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Boston" title="Sports in Boston">Sports in Boston</a></div>\n<p>Boston has teams in <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">the four major North American professional sports leagues</a> plus <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>, and has won 37 championships in these leagues, As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. It is one of five cities (along with Chicago, Los Angeles, New York and Philadelphia) to have won championships in all four major sports. It has been suggested<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> that Boston is the new "TitleTown, USA", as the city\'s professional sports teams have won ten championships since 2001: Patriots (2001, 2003, 2004, 2014, and 2016), Red Sox (2004, 2007, and 2013), Celtics (2008), and Bruins (2011). This love of sports made Boston the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" title="United States Olympic Committee">United States Olympic Committee</a>\'s choice to <a href="/wiki/Bids_for_Olympic_Games" title="Bids for Olympic Games">bid</a> to hold the <a href="/wiki/2024_Summer_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2024 Summer Olympic Games">2024 Summer Olympic Games</a>, but the city cited financial concerns when it withdrew its bid on July 27, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fenway_Park_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fenway_Park_2009.jpg/220px-Fenway_Park_2009.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fenway_Park_2009.jpg/330px-Fenway_Park_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fenway_Park_2009.jpg/440px-Fenway_Park_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4060" data-file-height="2680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fenway_Park_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_stadiums" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Major League Baseball stadiums">oldest</a> professional baseball stadium still in use.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> in 1901, play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Kenmore_Square" title="Kenmore Square">Kenmore Square</a> in the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Fenway-Kenmore" class="mw-redirect" title="Fenway-Kenmore">Fenway</a> section. Built in 1912, it is the oldest sports arena or stadium in active use in the United States among the four major professional American sports leagues, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Boston was the site of the first game of the first modern <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, in 1903. The series was played between the AL Champion <a href="/wiki/Boston_Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Americans">Boston Americans</a> and the NL champion <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Persistent reports that the team was known in 1903 as the "Boston Pilgrims" appear to be unfounded.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s first professional baseball team was the Red Stockings, one of the charter members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Professional_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Professional Base Ball Players">National Association</a> in 1871, and of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1876. The team played under that name until 1883, under the name Beaneaters until 1911, and under the name Braves from 1912 until they moved to <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a> after the 1952 season.
