Since 1966 they have played in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves,_February,_1_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Professional basketball game between the Celtics and Timberwolves in a crowded arena" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg/220px-Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg/330px-Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg/440px-Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves%2C_February%2C_1_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtics_game_versus_the_Timberwolves,_February,_1_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Celtics</a> play at the <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a>, formerly called the FleetCenter and built to replace the old, since-demolished <a href="/wiki/Boston_Garden" title="Boston Garden">Boston Garden</a>, is adjoined to <a href="/wiki/North_Station" title="North Station">North Station</a> and is the home of two major league teams: the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>. The arena seats 18,624 for basketball games and 17,565 for ice hockey games. The Bruins were the first American member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Original_Six" title="Original Six">Original Six</a> franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> The Boston Celtics were founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America" title="Basketball Association of America">Basketball Association of America</a>, one of the two leagues that merged to form the NBA.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The Celtics have the distinction of having won more championships than any other NBA team, with seventeen.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While they have played in suburban <a href="/wiki/Foxborough,_Massachusetts" title="Foxborough, Massachusetts">Foxborough</a> since 1971, the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> were founded in 1960 as the Boston Patriots, changing their name after relocating. The team won the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> after the 2001, 2003, 2004, 2014, and 2016 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> They share <a href="/wiki/Gillette_Stadium" title="Gillette Stadium">Gillette Stadium</a> with the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Revolution" title="New England Revolution">New England Revolution</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Breakers_(WPS)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Breakers (WPS)">Boston Breakers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Professional_Soccer" title="Women&#39;s Professional Soccer">Women\'s Professional Soccer</a>, which formed in 2009, play their home games at Dilboy Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-breakers-wps_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-breakers-wps-237">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Storm_(UWLX)" title="Boston Storm (UWLX)">Boston Storm</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Women%27s_Lacrosse_League" title="United Women&#39;s Lacrosse League">United Women\'s Lacrosse League</a> was formed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-storm-uwlx_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-storm-uwlx-238">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG/220px-Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG/330px-Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG/440px-Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="2946" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_stadium_2009h.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Stadium" title="Harvard Stadium">Harvard Stadium</a>, the first collegiate athletic stadium built in the U.S.</div></div></div>\n<p>The area\'s many colleges and universities are active in college athletics. Four <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> Division I members play in the city\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a>. Of the four, only Boston College participates in college football at the highest level, the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">Football Bowl Subdivision</a>. Harvard participates in the second-highest level, the <a href="/wiki/Football_Championship_Subdivision" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Championship Subdivision">Football Championship Subdivision</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Cannons" title="Boston Cannons">Boston Cannons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Lacrosse" title="Major League Lacrosse">MLL</a> play at Harvard Stadium.\n</p><p>One of the best known sporting events in the city is the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a>, the 26.2-mile (42.2&#160;km) race which is the world\'s oldest annual marathon,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> run on <a href="/wiki/Patriots%27_Day" title="Patriots&#39; Day">Patriots\' Day</a> in April. On April 15, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombing" title="Boston Marathon bombing">two explosions</a> killed three people and injured hundreds at the marathon.<sup id="cite_ref-260herald_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260herald-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\nAnother major annual event is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Charles_Regatta" title="Head of the Charles Regatta">Head of the Charles Regatta</a>, held in October.<sup id="cite_ref-hocr-harvard_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hocr-harvard-240">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_common_20060619.jpg" class="image"><img alt="City skyline with a body of water in the background and a green park in the foreground" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Boston_common_20060619.jpg/220px-Boston_common_20060619.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Boston_common_20060619.jpg/330px-Boston_common_20060619.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Boston_common_20060619.jpg/440px-Boston_common_20060619.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_common_20060619.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boston Common seen from the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Tower" title="Prudential Tower">Prudential Tower</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Boston_Common" title="Boston Common">Boston Common</a>, located near the Financial District and Beacon Hill, is the oldest public park in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris200561_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris200561-241">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Along with the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Public_Garden_(Boston)" title="Public Garden (Boston)">Boston Public Garden</a>, it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Emerald_Necklace" title="Emerald Necklace">Emerald Necklace</a>, a string of parks designed by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a> to encircle the city. The Emerald Necklace includes <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Pond" title="Jamaica Pond">Jamaica Pond</a>, Boston\'s largest body of freshwater, and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Park_(Boston)" title="Franklin Park (Boston)">Franklin Park</a>, the city\'s largest park and home of the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Park_Zoo" title="Franklin Park Zoo">Franklin Park Zoo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Another major park is the Esplanade, located along the banks of the Charles River. The <a href="/wiki/Hatch_Shell" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatch Shell">Hatch Shell</a>, an outdoor concert venue, is located adjacent to the Charles River Esplanade. Other parks are scattered throughout the city, with the major parks and beaches located near <a href="/wiki/Castle_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Castle Island (Massachusetts)">Castle Island</a>; in Charlestown; and along the Dorchester, South Boston, and East Boston shorelines.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston\'s park system is well-reputed nationally. In its 2013 ParkScore ranking, <a href="/wiki/Trust_for_Public_Land" class="mw-redirect" title="Trust for Public Land">The Trust for Public Land</a> reported that Boston was tied with <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> for having the third-best park system among the 50 most populous US cities.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> ParkScore ranks city park systems by a formula that analyzes the city\'s median park size, park acres as percent of city area, the percent of residents within a half-mile of a park, spending of park services per resident, and the number of playgrounds per 10,000 residents.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Boston_City_Hall" title="Boston City Hall">Boston City Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Emergency_Medical_Services" title="Boston Emergency Medical Services">Boston Emergency Medical Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Finance_Commission" title="Boston Finance Commission">Boston Finance Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Fire_Department" title="Boston Fire Department">Boston Fire Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Police_Department" title="Boston Police Department">Boston Police Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mayors of Boston">List of mayors of Boston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_Boston_City_Council" title="List of members of Boston City Council">List of members of Boston City Council</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Red brick building with white columns on the fa\xc3\xa7ade and a gold dome on the top" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg/220px-MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg/330px-MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg/440px-MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MA_State_House_11-13-2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_State_House" title="Massachusetts State House">Massachusetts State House</a>, seat of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Massachusetts" title="Government of Massachusetts">Government of Massachusetts</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Hill,_Boston" title="Beacon Hill, Boston">Beacon Hill</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Boston has a <a href="/wiki/Mayor%E2%80%93council_government" title="Mayor\xe2\x80\x93council government">strong mayor \xe2\x80\x93 council government</a> system in which the mayor (elected every fourth year) has extensive executive power. <a href="/wiki/Marty_Walsh_(politician)" title="Marty Walsh (politician)">Marty Walsh</a> became Mayor in January 2014, his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Menino" title="Thomas Menino">Thomas Menino</a>\'s twenty-year tenure having been the longest in the city\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Boston_City_Council" title="Boston City Council">Boston City Council</a> is elected every two years; there are nine district seats, and four citywide "at-large" seats.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> The School Committee, which oversees the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Schools" title="Boston Public Schools">Boston Public Schools</a>, is appointed by the mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to city government, numerous commissions and state authorities\xe2\x80\x94including the Massachusetts <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Conservation_and_Recreation" title="Department of Conservation and Recreation">Department of Conservation and Recreation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Health_Commission" title="Boston Public Health Commission">Boston Public Health Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Water_Resources_Authority" title="Massachusetts Water Resources Authority">Massachusetts Water Resources Authority (MWRA)</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Port_Authority" title="Massachusetts Port Authority">Massachusetts Port Authority (Massport)</a>\xe2\x80\x94play a role in the life of Bostonians. As the capital of Massachusetts, Boston plays a major role in <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts#Politics" title="Massachusetts">state politics</a>.\n</p><p>The city has several federal facilities, including the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Federal_Office_Building" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. Kennedy Federal Office Building">John F. Kennedy Federal Office Building</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_P._O%27Neill_Jr._Federal_Building_(Boston)" title="Thomas P. O&#39;Neill Jr. Federal Building (Boston)">Thomas P. O\'Neill Jr. Federal Building</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/John_W._McCormack_Post_Office_and_Courthouse" title="John W. McCormack Post Office and Courthouse">John W. McCormack Post Office and Courthouse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_Boston" title="Federal Reserve Bank of Boston">Federal Reserve Bank of Boston</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_First_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Massachusetts" title="United States District Court for the District of Massachusetts">United States District Court for the District of Massachusetts</a>. Both courts are housed in the <a href="/wiki/John_Joseph_Moakley_United_States_Courthouse" title="John Joseph Moakley United States Courthouse">John Joseph Moakley United States Courthouse</a>.\n</p><p>Federally, Boston is split between two congressional districts. The northern three-fourths of the city is in the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_7th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts&#39;s 7th congressional district">7th district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Capuano" title="Mike Capuano">Mike Capuano</a> since 1998. The southern fourth is in the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts&#39;s 8th congressional district">8th district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Lynch_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Lynch (politician)">Stephen Lynch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Both are Democrats; a Republican has not represented a significant portion of Boston in over a century. The state\'s senior member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> is Democrat <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a>, first elected in 2012. The state\'s junior member of the United States Senate is Democrat <a href="/wiki/Ed_Markey" title="Ed Markey">Ed Markey</a>, who was elected in 2013 to succeed <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> after Kerry\'s appointment and confirmation as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a>.\n</p><p>The city uses an algorithm created by the Walsh administration, called CityScore, to measure the effectiveness of various city services. This score is available on a public online dashboard and allows city managers in police, fire, schools, emergency management services, and <a href="/wiki/3-1-1" title="3-1-1">3-1-1</a> to take action and make adjustments in areas of concern.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Presidential election colspan="2">Total\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">387,040\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">100%\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Boston" title="Media in Boston">Media in Boston</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Herald" title="Boston Herald">Boston Herald</a></i> are two of the city\'s major daily newspapers. The city is also served by other publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_(magazine)" title="Boston (magazine)">Boston</a> magazine</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Improper_Bostonian" title="The Improper Bostonian">The Improper Bostonian</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/DigBoston" title="DigBoston">DigBoston</a></i>, and the Boston edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_International" title="Metro International">Metro</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">The Christian Science Monitor</a></i>, headquartered in Boston, was formerly a worldwide daily newspaper but ended publication of daily print editions in 2009, switching to continuous online and weekly magazine format publications.<sup id="cite_ref-csm-media_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm-media-253">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Boston Globe</i> also releases a teen publication to the city\'s public high schools, called <i>Teens in Print</i> or <i>T.i.P.</i>, which is written by the city\'s teens and delivered quarterly within the school year.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s growing <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a> population has given rise to a number of local and regional <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish-language</a> newspapers. These include <i><a href="/wiki/El_Planeta" title="El Planeta">El Planeta</a></i> (owned by the former publisher of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phoenix_(newspaper)" title="The Phoenix (newspaper)">The Boston Phoenix</a></i>), <i>El Mundo</i>, and <i>La Semana</i>. <i>Siglo21</i>, with its main offices in nearby <a href="/wiki/Lawrence,_Massachusetts" title="Lawrence, Massachusetts">Lawrence</a>, is also widely distributed.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are a number of weekly newspapers dedicated to Boston neighborhoods. Among them is South Boston Online, (founded in 1999) which appears in print and online, and covers events in South Boston and the Seaport District.\n</p><p>Various LGBT publications serve the city\'s large LGBT (lesbian, gay, bisexual, and transgender) population such as <i>The Rainbow Times</i>, the only minority and lesbian-owned LGBT news magazine. Founded in 2006, <i>The Rainbow Times</i> is now based out of Boston, but serves all of New England.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Boston is the largest broadcasting market in New England, with the radio market being the 9th largest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Several major <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> stations include <a href="/wiki/Talk_radio" title="Talk radio">talk radio</a> <a href="/wiki/WRKO" title="WRKO">WRKO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_radio" title="Sports radio">sports</a>/talk station <a href="/wiki/WEEI_(AM)" title="WEEI (AM)">WEEI</a>, and <a href="/wiki/CBS_Radio" title="CBS Radio">CBS Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/WBZ_(AM)" title="WBZ (AM)">WBZ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> WBZ (AM) broadcasts a <a href="/wiki/All-news_radio" title="All-news radio">news radio</a> format. A variety of commercial <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_format" title="Radio format">radio formats</a> serve the area, as do <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">NPR</a> stations <a href="/wiki/WBUR" class="mw-redirect" title="WBUR">WBUR</a> and <a href="/wiki/WGBH_(FM)" title="WGBH (FM)">WGBH</a>. College and university radio stations include <a href="/wiki/WERS" title="WERS">WERS</a> (Emerson), <a href="/wiki/WHRB" title="WHRB">WHRB</a> (Harvard), <a href="/wiki/WUMB" class="mw-redirect" title="WUMB">WUMB</a> (UMass Boston), <a href="/wiki/WMBR" title="WMBR">WMBR</a> (MIT), <a href="/wiki/WZBC" title="WZBC">WZBC</a> (Boston College), <a href="/wiki/WMFO" title="WMFO">WMFO</a> (Tufts University), <a href="/wiki/WBRS" title="WBRS">WBRS</a> (Brandeis University), <a href="/wiki/WTBU_(college_radio)" title="WTBU (college radio)">WTBU</a> (Boston University, campus and web only), <a href="/wiki/WRBB" title="WRBB">WRBB</a> (Northeastern University) and <a href="/wiki/WMLN-FM" title="WMLN-FM">WMLN-FM</a> (Curry College).\n</p><p>The Boston television <a href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Designated market area">DMA</a>, which also includes <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester, New Hampshire</a>, is the 8th largest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The city is served by stations representing every major <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_broadcast_television_networks" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United States broadcast television networks">American network</a>, including <a href="/wiki/WBZ-TV" title="WBZ-TV">WBZ-TV</a> 4 and its sister station <a href="/wiki/WSBK-TV" title="WSBK-TV">WSBK-TV</a> 38 (the former a <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> <a href="/wiki/Owned-and-operated_station" title="Owned-and-operated station">O&amp;O</a>, the latter an <a href="/wiki/MyNetwork_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="MyNetwork TV">MyNetwork TV</a> affiliate), <a href="/wiki/WCVB-TV" title="WCVB-TV">WCVB-TV</a> 5 and its sister station <a href="/wiki/WMUR-TV" title="WMUR-TV">WMUR-TV</a> 9 (both <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>), <a href="/wiki/WHDH_(TV)" title="WHDH (TV)">WHDH</a> 7 and its sister station <a href="/wiki/WLVI" title="WLVI">WLVI</a> 56 (the former an <a href="/wiki/Independent_station_(North_America)" title="Independent station (North America)">independent station</a>, the latter a <a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">CW</a> affiliate), <a href="/wiki/WBTS-LD" title="WBTS-LD">WBTS-LD</a> 8 (a <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> O&amp;O), and <a href="/wiki/WFXT-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="WFXT-TV">WFXT</a> 25 (<a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>). The city is also home to <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> member station <a href="/wiki/WGBH-TV" title="WGBH-TV">WGBH-TV</a> 2, a major producer of PBS programs,<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> which also operates <a href="/wiki/WGBX" class="mw-redirect" title="WGBX">WGBX</a> 44. Spanish-language television networks, including <a href="/wiki/Azteca_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Azteca (TV network)">Azteca</a> (<a href="/wiki/WFXZ-CD" title="WFXZ-CD">WFXZ-CD</a> 24), <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">Univision</a> (<a href="/wiki/WUNI" title="WUNI">WUNI</a> 27), <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">Telemundo</a> (<a href="/wiki/WNEU" title="WNEU">WNEU</a> 60, a sister station to WBTS-LD), and <a href="/wiki/UniM%C3%A1s" title="UniM\xc3\xa1s">UniM\xc3\xa1s</a> (<a href="/wiki/WUTF-DT" class="mw-redirect" title="WUTF-DT">WUTF-DT</a> 66), have a presence in the region, with <a href="/wiki/WNEU" title="WNEU">WNEU</a> and <a href="/wiki/WUTF" class="mw-redirect" title="WUTF">WUTF</a> serving as network <a href="/wiki/Owned-and-operated_station" title="Owned-and-operated station">owned-and-operated stations</a>. Most of the area\'s television stations have their transmitters in nearby <a href="/wiki/Needham,_Massachusetts" title="Needham, Massachusetts">Needham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newton,_Massachusetts" title="Newton, Massachusetts">Newton</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_128" title="Massachusetts Route 128">Route 128 corridor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Six Boston television stations are carried by Canadian satellite television provider Bell TV and by cable television providers in Canada.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Boston_in_fiction#Film" title="Boston in fiction">List of movies filmed in Boston</a></div>\n<p>Films have been made in Boston since as early as 1903, and it continues to be both a popular setting and a popular site for location shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Massachusetts#Boston" title="List of hospitals in Massachusetts">List of hospitals in Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardMed2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/HarvardMed2.JPG/220px-HarvardMed2.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/HarvardMed2.JPG/330px-HarvardMed2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/HarvardMed2.JPG/440px-HarvardMed2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarvardMed2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School" title="Harvard Medical School">Harvard Medical School</a>, one of the most prestigious medical schools in the world</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Longwood_Medical_and_Academic_Area" title="Longwood Medical and Academic Area">Longwood Medical and Academic Area</a>, adjacent to the Fenway district, is home to a large number of medical and research facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Beth_Israel_Deaconess_Medical_Center" title="Beth Israel Deaconess Medical Center">Beth Israel Deaconess Medical Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brigham_and_Women%27s_Hospital" title="Brigham and Women&#39;s Hospital">Brigham and Women\'s Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Boston Children&#39;s Hospital">Boston Children\'s Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dana%E2%80%93Farber_Cancer_Institute" title="Dana\xe2\x80\x93Farber Cancer Institute">Dana\xe2\x80\x93Farber Cancer Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School" title="Harvard Medical School">Harvard Medical School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joslin_Diabetes_Center" title="Joslin Diabetes Center">Joslin Diabetes Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/MCPHS_University" title="MCPHS University">Massachusetts College of Pharmacy and Health Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>\nProminent medical facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Hospital" title="Massachusetts General Hospital">Massachusetts General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Eye_and_Ear_Infirmary" class="mw-redirect" title="Massachusetts Eye and Ear Infirmary">Massachusetts Eye and Ear Infirmary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spaulding_Rehabilitation_Hospital" title="Spaulding Rehabilitation Hospital">Spaulding Rehabilitation Hospital</a> are located in the Beacon Hill area. <a href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth%27s_Medical_Center_(Boston)" title="St. Elizabeth&#39;s Medical Center (Boston)">St. Elizabeth\'s Medical Center</a> is in Brighton Center of the city\'s Brighton neighborhood. <a href="/wiki/New_England_Baptist_Hospital" title="New England Baptist Hospital">New England Baptist Hospital</a> is in Mission Hill. <a href="/wiki/VA_Boston_Healthcare_System" title="VA Boston Healthcare System">The city has Veterans Affairs medical centers</a> in the Jamaica Plain and West Roxbury neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Health_Commission" title="Boston Public Health Commission">Boston Public Health Commission</a>, an agency of the Massachusetts government, oversees health concerns for city residents.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boston_EMS" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston EMS">Boston EMS</a> provides pre-hospital emergency medical services to residents and visitors.\n</p><p>Many of Boston\'s medical facilities are associated with universities. The facilities in the Longwood Medical and Academic Area and in Massachusetts General Hospital are affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Medical_School" title="Harvard Medical School">Harvard Medical School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tufts_Medical_Center" title="Tufts Medical Center">Tufts Medical Center</a> (formerly Tufts-New England Medical Center), located in the southern portion of the Chinatown neighborhood, is affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Tufts University School of Medicine">Tufts University School of Medicine</a>. <a href="/wiki/Boston_Medical_Center" title="Boston Medical Center">Boston Medical Center</a>, located in the South End neighborhood, is the primary teaching facility for the <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Boston University School of Medicine">Boston University School of Medicine</a> as well as the largest trauma center in the Boston area;<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> it was formed by the merger of Boston University Hospital and Boston City Hospital, which was the first municipal hospital in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_in_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Infrastructure in Boston">Infrastructure in Boston</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Boston" title="Transportation in Boston">Transportation in Boston</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthStation.agr.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/SouthStation.agr.JPG/220px-SouthStation.agr.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/SouthStation.agr.JPG/330px-SouthStation.agr.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/SouthStation.agr.JPG/440px-SouthStation.agr.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthStation.agr.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a>, the busiest rail hub in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, is a terminus of <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Transportation_Authority" title="Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority">MBTA</a> rail lines.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A silver and red rapid transit train departing an above-ground station" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg/220px-RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg/330px-RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg/440px-RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RedLineCharlesMGH.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(MBTA)" title="Red Line (MBTA)">MBTA Red Line</a> train departing Boston for Cambridge. Bostonians depend heavily on public transit, with over 1.3 million Bostonians riding the city\'s buses and trains daily (2013).<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg/220px-Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg/330px-Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg/440px-Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2948" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hubway_bikes_at_rack.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Blue_Bikes" title="Blue Bikes">Hubway</a> bikes in Boston</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan Airport</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/East_Boston" title="East Boston">East Boston</a> and operated by the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Port_Authority" title="Massachusetts Port Authority">Massachusetts Port Authority (Massport)</a>, is Boston\'s principal airport.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Nearby <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> airports are <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Municipal_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Municipal Airport">Beverly Municipal Airport</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Hanscom_Field" title="Hanscom Field">Hanscom Field</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Memorial_Airport" title="Norwood Memorial Airport">Norwood Memorial Airport</a> to the south. Massport also operates several major facilities within the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Boston" title="Port of Boston">Port of Boston</a>, including a cruise ship terminal and facilities to handle bulk and container cargo in <a href="/wiki/South_Boston" title="South Boston">South Boston</a>, and other facilities in <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Boston" title="Charlestown, Boston">Charlestown</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Boston" title="East Boston">East Boston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston,_MA_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg/220px-Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg/330px-Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg/440px-Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston%2C_MA_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2092" data-file-height="1849" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Bridge_-_Boston,_MA_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonard_P._Zakim_Bunker_Hill_Memorial_Bridge" title="Leonard P. Zakim Bunker Hill Memorial Bridge">Leonard P. Zakim Bunker Hill Memorial Bridge</a> crosses the <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a> from <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Boston" title="Downtown Boston">Downtown Boston</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Downtown Boston\'s streets grew organically, so they do not form a <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">planned grid</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> unlike those in later-developed <a href="/wiki/Back_Bay,_Boston" title="Back Bay, Boston">Back Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Boston" title="East Boston">East Boston</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_End,_Boston" title="South End, Boston">South End</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Boston,_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="South Boston, Boston">South Boston</a>. Boston is the eastern terminus of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_90" title="Interstate 90">I-90</a>, which in Massachusetts runs along the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Turnpike" title="Massachusetts Turnpike">Massachusetts Turnpike</a>. The elevated portion of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Artery" title="Central Artery">Central Artery</a>, which carried most of the through traffic in downtown Boston, was replaced with the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_P._O%27Neill_Jr._Tunnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas P. O&#39;Neill Jr. Tunnel">O\'Neill Tunnel</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Big_Dig" title="Big Dig">Big Dig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Construction_management#Post-Construction" title="Construction management">substantially completed</a> in early 2006.\n</p><p>With nearly a third of Bostonians using public transit for their commute to work, Boston has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_with_high_transit_ridership" title="List of U.S. cities with high transit ridership">fifth-highest rate of public transit usage in the country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> The city of Boston has a higher than average percentage of households without a car. In 2015, 35.4 percent of Boston households lacked a car, which decreased slightly to 33.8 percent in 2016. The national average was 8.7 percent in 2016. Boston averaged 0.94 cars per household in 2016, compared to a national average of 1.8.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Boston\'s subway system, the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Transportation_Authority" title="Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority">Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority</a> (MBTA\xe2\x80\x94known as the "T") operates the oldest underground rapid transit system in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_rapid_transit_systems_by_ridership" title="List of United States rapid transit systems by ridership">fourth-busiest rapid transit system in the country</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHull201142_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHull201142-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> with 65.5 miles (105&#160;km) of track on four lines.<sup id="cite_ref-light_rail_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-light_rail-276">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The MBTA also operates busy bus and commuter rail networks, and water shuttles.<sup id="cite_ref-light_rail_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-light_rail-276">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a> and Chicago lines originate at <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a>, which serves as a major <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_passenger_transport" title="Intermodal passenger transport">intermodal transportation</a> hub, and stop at <a href="/wiki/Back_Bay_station" title="Back Bay station">Back Bay</a>. Fast Northeast Corridor trains, which serve New York City, Washington, D.C., and points in between, also stop at <a href="/wiki/Route_128_station" title="Route 128 station">Route 128 Station</a> in the southwestern suburbs of Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, Amtrak\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">Downeaster</a></i> service to <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> originates at <a href="/wiki/North_Station" title="North Station">North Station</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> despite <a href="/wiki/North-South_Rail_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="North-South Rail Link">the current lack of a dedicated passenger rail link</a> between the two railhubs, other than the "T" subway lines.\n</p><p>Nicknamed "The Walking City", Boston hosts more pedestrian commuters than do other comparably populated cities. Owing to factors such as necessity, the compactness of the city and large student population, 13 percent of the population commutes by foot, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_with_most_pedestrian_commuters" title="List of U.S. cities with most pedestrian commuters">highest percentage of pedestrian commuters in the country</a> out of the major American cities.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Walk_Score" title="Walk Score">Walk Score</a> ranked Boston the third most walkable city in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> As of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Walk Score still ranks Boston as the third most walkable US city, with a Walk Score of 80, a Transit Score of 75, and a Bike Score of 70.<sup id="cite_ref-WalkScore_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalkScore-282">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1999 and 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Bicycling_(magazine)" title="Bicycling (magazine)">Bicycling</a></i> magazine named Boston three times as one of the worst cities in the US for cycling;<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> regardless, it has one of the highest rates of bicycle commuting.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, as a consequence of improvements made to bicycling conditions within the city, the same magazine put Boston on its "Five for the Future" list as a "Future Best City" for biking,<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> and Boston\'s bicycle commuting percentage increased from 1% in 2000 to 2.1% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The bikeshare program called <a href="/wiki/Hubway" class="mw-redirect" title="Hubway">Hubway</a> launched in late July 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> logging more than 140,000 rides before the close of its first season.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> The neighboring municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brookline,_Massachusetts" title="Brookline, Massachusetts">Brookline</a> joined the Hubway program in the summer of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, there are 1,461 bikes and 158 docking stations across the city.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PBSC_Urban_Solutions" title="PBSC Urban Solutions">PBSC Urban Solutions</a> provides bicycles and technology for this <a href="/wiki/Bicycle-sharing_system" title="Bicycle-sharing system">bike-sharing system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, the Boston-Cambridge-Newton metropolitan statistical area (Boston MSA) had the seventh-lowest percentage of workers who commuted by private automobile (75.6 percent), with 6.2 percent of area workers traveling via rail transit. During the period starting in 2006 and ending in 2013, the Boston MSA had the greatest percentage decline of workers commuting by automobile (3.3 percent) among MSAs with more than a half-million residents.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister href="/wiki/Bellville,_Western_Cape" title="Bellville, Western Cape">Bellville, Western Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and developed it for residential purposes. In memory of their hometown, they called it <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Bellville" title="Boston, Bellville">Boston</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span href="/w/index.php?title=Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">New Style</a> (modern) calendar, anniversaries fall on September 17.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">New Style</a> (modern) calendar, anniversaries of the original Old Style date fall on September 17.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The average number of days with a low at or below freezing is 94.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Seasonal snowfall accumulation has ranged from 9.0&#160;in (22.9&#160;cm) in 1936\xe2\x80\x9337 to 110.6&#160;in (2.81&#160;m) in 2014\xe2\x80\x9315.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the expected highest and lowest temperature readings at any point during the year or given month) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Official records for Boston were kept at downtown from January 1872 to December 1935, and at Logan Airport (KBOS) since January 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-ThreadEx_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThreadEx-111">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
